<review>Get ready to be enchanted.  This is one of the finest restaurants anywhere.  They have everything right.  And not one ingredient is in its original form - something creative has made each one special - even the garnishes.

A warm welcoming decor that's casual and elegant all at once.  The personnel introduce themselves without the "I'm your waiter Bob" line and not necessarily on the encounter.

I ordered a Pisco Sour, the national drink of Peru.  Pisco (a Peruvian Brandy), lemon juice, simple syrup and then egg whites that provide a smooth foam.  On par with the best I've had in Lima.

Then to the yellowtail ceviche.  Perfectly cut, not a hint of connective tissue and a sublime marinade with tiger milk, sliced red onion and nuts to add some crunch.  Beautifully served in glazed handmade pottery.

On to Panacota for dessert.  Add toasted quinoa sprinkled on top and have it sit in fermented honey, then artfully place pieces of what they call "Forest" on top.  They look like shaved bark, they have some crunch and the taste is mildly sweet and savory - a wonderful accompaniment to the not overly sweet dish.

Bottom line.  A winner any way you want to measure a restaurant.< /review>< userid>
104745565929433688409<//userid>

<user>105681880633417703199< /user><username>Helen Arens</username><date>1620514995836<//date><Rate>5</Rate><review>This little gem is easy to miss, tucked in the middle of a nondescript strip mall along busy McFadden Avenue.  But do yourself a favor and stop in.  The friendly owner will explain what is in all the exotically named yummy looking sweets, kebabs and meat pastries, all very reasonably priced.  They make it all themselves, so the baklava is truly fresh, not all dried out like most places that buy it pre-made.  Try the sujuk (also known as kachapuri), a large pastry shell filled with eggs and thin-sliced beef.  There are a few tables inside and one table outside, so you  can eat in or take out.</review>< Pics>

Located in an unassuming strip mall, the place is tiny, spare, and does not have AC. On a sweltering weekend afternoon it could be likened to a circle of hell, if not for the heavenly food coming out of the kitchen. Poor Jack was just sweating BUCKETS but still had a wide welcoming smile and treated us like gold. We got an order of the spinach calzone-like things (forget the name) and a falafel plate that came with hummus, pita, and various pickled things. Pretty standard fare, right? Not in Jack's hands: his falafels are the BEST I've ever had--donut-shaped, which was a little odd, but very light and fluffy! Often I'm disappointed by leaden falafels, but not these guys. Everything else was great too but that falafel, wow. I'm drooling just thinking about them! Now that the weather's cooling off it might be a better time to visit; if you haven't already, do so posthaste! < Text>
I love the Rock Church whether I am there or online.  Every week is different. Each week is different and we can't wait to get there the next week.  Plenty of parking but for the good spots you need to get there early.  They have an area where families with young children are allowed to park.  Handicapped accessible.  Many activities are planned for everyone.  The only problem we have is when you need to call someone whether it's a pastor or just to ask a question you can NEVER reach anyone, not even a call back after a message is left.  Yes everyone is friendly & pleasant but sometimes it's nice if the Pastor(s) could just hang around and kind of meet & greet after service...makes me feel that the church is getting too big to go back to the beginning. Other than that I love this church but feel they need to go back whence they started.</Text>

<UserId.>109792752950071197236<//UserId.><name>Miracle Worker< /name><gmap_id>0x80deab070dcbc45d:0x6c8b55d194b706a<//gmap_id>< Response>

< review>
Witnessed a softball practice by what I presume is this team as the shirts were labeled "Rock" and "Warriors".  The practice was at the Balboa Park  Athletics side on the baseball diamonds this morning between 11am -12pm today. I had just completed my workout and decided to watch the practice session for a few minutes. As soon as I sat down on the bleachers someone who appears to be the Coach yelled:  "Alright you little monkey catch this." He followed that action by hitting the ball to the player he deemed the "Monkey".
Immediately the players in the outfield and infield retorted the coaches actions by stating:  "Hey coach you think that's a little racist."
So I am watching this entire incident awestruck by what was taking place in a completely public forum. Well, it gets worse.  I initially thought these were a bunch of 20 somethings enjoying their sports day. These people turned out to be 14,15, 16 year olds.

That's when things changed for me. So I sat there a little longer than scheduled,  to see what else I could uncover about the coach and the program and any other underlying issues.  After careful and thoughtful research this is how I decided to report this issue as Rock Academy phones don't answer.

About the Rock Academy
"Bringing the Living Word to students in order to lead them into a personal relationship with Christ; we diligently equip them with the educational, spiritual, social and physical tools needed to become Christian leaders."

While I can't judge Rock Academy based on this single incident, I will state without any reservations or doubt that today's incident is not consistent with the above statement I pulled from the website or the Mission Statement all together. I know sometimes we tend to belittle issues like this to further the "Bigger Picture" and I hope that is not the end result.  I've spent 15 years in education and recruiting and as a recruiter I am taught to read body language and facial expressions.  These young boys are completely damaged mentally and psychologically by someone who is supposed to be the guardian of their well being.  The Coach, the mentor, the teacher failed today.

So as the coach yelled "Monkey" the young man assigned to catch the balls as they are being thrown back in from the outfield stated maturely: "Monkey coach, you think that's a little racist?"
Coach stated under his breath but loud enough for me to here : "Like I told you before any race can be a monkey." That is the lesson learned today at the Rock Academy an affiliation of Rock Church.

As they players rallied in to take their turn at hitting I kept an eye out for the Middle Fielder, the kid he called monkey just to see if he was okay mentally and it turns out he was a very young man of Latino descent. In fact, the entire team, as presented today is varied in its racial make-up.

Not surprised but shocked for these kids who are being made to endure this verbal abuse by someone whom I presume has been vetted by key members of the Rock Academy and Rock Church.< /review>

<Date>1413735108517</Date><Rate>5</Rate><review>I have been going to the Rock Church for 5 years, and it has been good for me.  The church is HUGE.  Because of this you must make an effort if you want to be involved.  I have been to many small churches in the past where they have you stand and introduce yourself the first time you visit.  This is NOT that kind of church, it is a mega church.  I like it because it is as personal as you want to make it.  If you want to attend, sit back, and listen to the message, that is fine.  There is no pressure.  If you want to be more involved with a smaller group, there is one for EVERYONE.  Everything from prison ministry, single parents, dog lovers, sewing, you name it- there is a group for it.  This can make it overwhelming, but if you take time to attend and talk to people, you will find a group that speaks to your heart.  All of the pastors I have met are great; very down to Earth (no pun intended).  The worship is amazing!   No judgement in this church, come as you are, and enjoy the Word.< /review>< Pics>

I have been going to the Rock Church in San Diego for over 3 years and it has been a true blessing for my walk. Pastor Miles is a wonderful funny and energetic speaker who inspires thousands to take their Faith into action by serving in a ministry, participating in a Do Something event, connecting in small group, discipleship, and just simple worshiping God.

<review>PARKING/LOCATION: On Sundays, depending on which time you visit, you can get very lucky and park really close, or have to park really far and just walk. Located near Vons, Panera Bread, Starbucks, and other great restaurants in Liberty Station, the church brings in a good stream of business for its neighbors throughout the week, not just on Sundays.

WALKING THROUGH THE DOORS FOR THE FIRST TIME: I imagine someone new to the Rock church or just visiting will feel extremely overwhelmed when they first walk inside. Don't expect it to look very "church-y" because it's more of a building than a typical church where you'd expect to see a huge crucifix hanging on the wall. We've got that too but it's displayed very differently here. ;)

STRAIGHT AHEAD: Past the entrance doors, if the service will be doing a communion that Sunday, you'll notice a table with buckets filled with little communion cups (of grape juice and a wafer). Grab one if you plan on attending service. Past that, you'll immediately be standing inside the building's lobby and welcome/reception area. Behind this welcome/reception area are the elevators which can take you to the second and third floors of the sanctuary. (There are also stairs.) Past the elevators on the bottom floor, to your right is the church bookstore, and behind the bookstore is an area to eat at D'Lush. Past that you will be reaching the backside of the church. A nice little park area with astroturf grass, and a playground up top.

TO YOUR LEFT: The main sanctuary. The sanctuary has 2 doorways on the bottom and top floors. If there is worship going on, you can view it from the LCD screens (on the bottom floor) they have hanging against the left wall (in front of the sanctuary), and you'll notice people starting to walk inside, as they are being greeted by an usher/greeter and handed a lesson plan/bulletin. Just before entering the main sanctuary though (you can even ask an usher/greeter) there is a room reserved for nursing moms, and a TV which broadcasts a live feed of the service happening in the sanctuary. Pretty nice and quiet. Gentle area with some soft seats/sofas... changing area, etc.

TO YOUR RIGHT: To your immediate right is the entrance way to the Children's Ministry, where parents can drop off their kids and have them learn what they learn, but at their age level. Plan on coming early if you are thinking of bringing your kids here. Typically, no kids under the age of 5 are allowed in the main sanctuary so plan accordingly. :)  Past the bookstore to your right, is the entrance way to the cafeteria area. I haven't been there lately during service, but I used to attend service in the cafeteria area (watching it broadcast live on TV on both sides). Great place to catch service while you eat if you haven't had breakfast or lunch yet. Not sure if this has changed, but if not, there should also be an usher/greeter at the front of this entrance as well. :)

THE EXPERIENCE: The experience is different for everyone. It really depends on you. To get the most out of it, you really want to have an open heart and mind once entering the sanctuary. Don't worry about anyone else around you. This is going to be YOUR time with God. No one else should fit into that equation. Prepare yourself for whatever message the pastor will be teaching that Sunday, and even if you may not believe in God (yet?), know that His presence is everywhere. It wouldn't hurt to ask whoever this God is that's got so many Rock church goers ALIVE IN HIM to "speak" to you through the message that day. Made the decision to follow Jesus? Contact me!<//review>< date>
1422478639668</date>

<rate>2<//rate><text>Back in july i took our frenchie there because he had severe diarrhea and ended up staying there for 5 days. He had no other symptoms so my first thought is salmonella since he did eat cooked chicken before. Turns out he had nothing wrong, no infection nor bacteria ( which made no sense). At pick up i was given antibiotics incase he did have something and that seemed to have been working for him there i guess ( still not making sense). So on my way to the car he coughs and im like "okay" this better not be kennel cough because he didn't have it before". I get home and he's coughing more and i wait a day or two before i call the clinic to make sure it's not a dry throat. They prescribe clavamox and temaril over the phone. So im thinking ok this should work since it just started. I notice neither meds is working but i wait to finish the temaril since it helps open the airways. Let me say i have always worked as a vet tech since i was 17 and stopped about 5-6 yrs ago cuz i had to raise my son. And i know if the meds aren't working its because its beyond just a cough now. I take him back and i tell them i recieved him back sicker, turns out it was a respiratory infection almost turning into broncolitis. Both lungs and heart were inflamed. I was upset because kennel cough is the cause for this and kennel cough is airborne. Meaning the dog who had it wasn't isolated from other dogs or the clinic lacks in sanitizing the exam rooms. I mentioned it to the doc and was given a discount. And to top it off his cough lasted 2 months.
This shouldn't have gone unnoticed, when you are in treatment medicating and observing the pets that stay over night your job is to mention it on the file but it wasn't. This is very irresponsible that means this place isn't being run correctly. Every vet i have ever worked at has one big rule which is " always clean the exam room before and after" and sanitize the floors often and that's something colima does not do. My heart sanked because i know breeders who have gone to colima and had their pups died from a bad respiratory infection.  But we had not experienced it yet up until that day. I understand you techs at colima are busy but a way to make it easier and smoother for everyone is to do what's easy first.
Vaccines, deworming, and progesterone test should be seen first. You don't need to take them to the back or to a room, it can be done in the car or up front. Medication, drop off and pick up can be done by two or 3 girls. And last should be the dogs waiting for an exam. This way things are out of the way and so are people.< /text>< Pics>

DO NOT GO TO THIS VET IF YOUR PET HAS AN URGENT MEDICAL CONDITION.

This vet appears to primarily serve the birthing of french bulldog puppies -- if your pet needs medical attention, like my cat did, DO NOT COME HERE.
In addition to their general rude attitude, long waits, and disorganization, which would be ordinarily excusable if the medical service was effective... It is not effective nor a good place to get medical services for your pet.

They botched my cat's surgery which should have been a simple operation. He is now going onto his 2nd month of recovery from what should have been a 2-week operation.
The staff was completely clueless when it came to what we needed to do at home, they didn't provide us with a cone or medication, leaving us to do the guesswork and Google what needs to be done post-operation.

Your pets deserve better!< /Review>

< Text>
We had a very poor experience at this vet from 9/27/2020 to 9/28/2020. We adopted a puppy from a local rescue, and this was the rescue's choice for spay. We were told to show up early and got to the vet at 7am, we didn't leave until 9 am because of the process and the amount of dogs. We were expecting to pick up our dog that night. We called to check up on her several times, but were told they hadn't started yet and to call back again. We called at 8:30 (they close at 7) and were told they still hadn't started the spay! We asked if we could take our dog home for the night and bring her back the next morning, and we told her they were going to fix her that night and she'd be ready at 11am the next day. Big surprise! Our dog was not ready at 11am, like promised. We called them again around 3 and was told she still was not spayed. We even called the rescue and they agreed that this was unprofessional. The vet couldn't even tell the rescue an approximate time of surgery. The vet's excuse was that if emergencies came in they had to attend to them frist. Don't get me wrong, I do agree emergencies have some priority, but in our case our dog had already been with them for more that 30 hours, she needed to be the priority. At this point we were driving to the vet to pick her up regardless, because we were no longer confident in this vet. Due to traffic and the fact we were coming from Long Beach, we picked her up at 5, and she had suddenly been spayed. Finally.

Our dog sat in this vet's care for over 30 hours for a simple spay. She was not allowed to eat the night before and because they kept intending to do the surgery that day/night she was not allowed to eat or drink for over 40 hours. The employees there did not even apologize or acknowledge they they took so long to do the procedure.

The other reviews about this vet being involved with many bully breeders is true, when we picked up our dog, there were several bullies waiting for c-sections. While I was waiting to get our puppy the staff was also very rude to the other people waiting to be seen.

Unless you're a bully breeder, I would go elsewhere.</Text>
